# Notes
# 1. This is a list of people (rather than a list of isolated names) taken from CUDL. You may find more. Please add them.
# 2. I've attempted to un-anglicize all the Hebrew names. I may not have gotten them all; if you find one, please correct it with a global find-replace, or else post a question to the #names-and-dates channel on Slack.
# 3. Anglicized titles remain, e.g., Natan ha-Levi he-Ḥaver the Adept b. Yeshuʿa. At some point we'll might want to track down the documents and re-semiticize them, but probably not all the ones on the list: since the list is taken from CUDL, it includes literary fragments that we don't track in PGP.
# 4. Two special cases: Yaʿqūb/Yaʿaqov and Yūsuf/Yosef are spelled the exact same way in Hebrew and JA. How, then, to de-anglicize the name? I've taken the following approach, which is admittedly a bit arbitrary (or completely unfalsifiable), but which I prefer to Jacob and Joseph: if there is an obviously Hebrew element in the name (patronymic, ha-Kohen, ha-Levi, gaʾon), I went with Hebrew; if there was an obviously Arabic element (e.g., a kunya, like Abū Naṣr), I went with Arabic.
# 5. The second tab contains names (rather than people) found in PGP. The list hasn't yet been fully cleaned. At some point we may want to add them into this list, but it's more likely that we'll extract names of real people from PGP. I've put it here to keep all the info in one place."
